# Text Elements
The subsonic compressible flow over a cosine-shaped (wavy) wall is illustrated in Figure ^5A3FrNOQ

2.17. The wavelength and amplitude of the wall are l and h, respectively, as shown ^R6qgU4F1

in Figure 2.17. The streamlines exhibit the same qualitative shape as the wall, but with ^rVewmAld

diminishing amplitude as distance above the wall increases. Finally, as y →   , the ^Tg6xD0FX

streamline becomes straight. Along this straight streamline, the freestream velocity and ^Qmp2oHLG

Mach number are     and     , respectively. The velocity field in cartesian coordinates ^YCXaYiiK

is given by ^OlstEeki

where ^jvAwMWHX

l = 1.0 m, h = 0.01 m,    = ^ib0vYCBH

Consider the particular flow that exists for the case where ^juUU8Gw3

240 m/s, and      = 0.7. Also, consider a fluid element of fixed mass moving along a ^uutCGSlu

streamline in the flowfield. The fluid element passes through the point (x/l , y/l) = (1/4,1) ^vqPilXOY

At this point, calculate the time rate of change of the volume of the fluid element, per unit ^qpNeR9Ri

volume. ^PKcrdH28

Solution:  ^RiYqQ4Z5

we firstly calculate the u, v and then calculate  ^PPG8bpAF

the  ^r6Zf7XyK

We note that the curl of the velocity is not zero, thus it's a
compressible flow.  ^Kcz9EHMR
